A T1 Weighted Dynamic Contrast Enhanced MR image reflects the dynamics of diffusion of the exogenous contrast media from the blood pool into the extra vascular extracellular space (EES) of the brain at a rate determined by the blood flow to the tissue, the permeability of the Brain Blood Barrier (BBB), and the surface area of the perfusing vessels.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"110817\">110817</a></td>\n        <td>T2 Weighted Dynamic Contrast Enhanced MR Signal Intensity</td>\n        <td>Signal intensity of a T2 Weighted Dynamic Contrast Enhanced MR image.  </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"113064\">113064</a></td>\n        <td>T2* Map</td>\n        <td>The image is derived by calculating T2* values.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"113065\">113065</a></td>\n        <td>T2 Map</td>\n        <td>The image is derived by calculating T2 values.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"113066\">113066</a></td>\n        <td>Time Course of Signal</td>\n        <td>The image is derived by calculating values based on the time course of signal.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"113067\">113067</a></td>\n        <td>Temperature encoded</td>\n        <td>The image is derived by calculating values based on temperature encoding.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"113068\">113068</a></td>\n        <td>Student’s T-Test</td>\n        <td>The image is derived by calculating the value of the Student’s T-Test statistic from multiple image samples.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"113069\">113069</a></td>\n        <td>Time To Peak map</td>\n        <td>The image is derived by calculating values based on the time to encoded (e.g., phase contrast).</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"113071\">113071</a></td>\n        <td>Z-Score Map</td>\n        <td>The image is derived by calculating the value of the Z-Score statistic from multiple image samples.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"113072\">113072</a></td>\n        <td>Multiplanar reformatting</td>\n        <td>The image is derived by reformatting in a flat plane other than that originally acquired.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"113073\">113073</a></td>\n        <td>Curved multiplanar </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122325\">122325</a></td>\n        <td>IVUS Report</td>\n        <td>Intravascular Ultrasound Report</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122330\">122330</a></td>\n        <td>EEM Diameter</td>\n        <td>External Elastic Membrane (EEM) diameter measured through the center point of the vessel. Center point of the vessel is defined as the center of gravity of the EEM area. The EEM is a discrete interface at the border between the media and the adventitia.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122331\">122331</a></td>\n        <td>Plaque Plus Media Thickness</td>\n        <td>The distance from intimal leading edge to the external elastic membrane along any line passing through the luminal center, which is defined as the center of gravity of the lumen area.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122332\">122332</a></td>\n        <td>Lumen Perimeter</td>\n        <td>Planimetered perimeter of the lumen.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122333\">122333</a></td>\n        <td>EEM Cross-Sectional Area</td>\n        <td>Vessel area measured at the External Elastic Membrane (EEM), a discrete interface at the border between the media and the adventitia.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122334\">122334</a></td>\n        <td>Plaque plus Media Cross-Sectional Area</td>\n        <td>Area within the EEM occupied by atheroma, regardless of lumen compromise. Plaque plus Media Area = EEM cross-sectional area - vessel lumen cross-sectional area</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122335\">122335</a></td>\n        <td>In-Stent Neointimal Cross-Sectional Area</td>\n        <td>Measurement of in-stent restenosis. In-Stent Intimal Area = Stent cross-sectional area – vessel lumen cross-sectional area</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122336\">122336</a></td>\n        <td>Vascular Volume measurement length</td>\n        <td>Longitudinal extent of the Vascular Volume Measurement. This is the distance from the distal edge to the proximal edge of the Volume measurement.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122337\">122337</a></td>\n        <td>Relative position</td>\n        <td>Longitudinal distance from the closest edge of a fiducial feature or reference location to the start of the vascular measurement. This value will be a positive if the measurement is distal to the fiducial feature or reference location, or negative if the measurement is proximal to the fiducial feature or reference location.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122339\">122339</a></td>\n        <td>Stent Volume Obstruction</td>\n        <td>In-Stent Neointimal Volume / Stent Volume</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122340\">122340</a></td>\n        <td>Fiducial feature</td>\n        <td>Reference, normally anatomical, which is used for locating the position of a measurement.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122341\">122341</a></td>\n        <td>Calcium Length</td>\n        <td>Longitudinal calcium length measurement</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122343\">122343</a></td>\n        <td>Lumen Eccentricity Index</td>\n        <td>Measurement of vessel lumen eccentricity. Lumen Eccentricity Index = (maximum vessel lumen diameter - minimum vessel lumen diameter) / maximum vessel lumen diameter. Lumen diameters are measured through the center point of the lumen, which is defined as the center of gravity of the lumen area.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122344\">122344</a></td>\n        <td>Plaque plus Media Eccentricity Index</td>\n        <td>Plaque plus Media Eccentricity Index  = (maximum Plaque plus media thickness - minimum Plaque plus media thickness) / maximum Plaque plus media thickness</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122345\">122345</a></td>\n        <td>Remodeling Index</td>\n        <td>Measurement of increase or decrease in EEM area that occurs during the development of atherosclerosis. Remodeling Index = Lesion EEM area / reference EEM area</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122346\">122346</a></td>\n        <td>Stent Symmetry Index</td>\n        <td>Measurement of stent circularity. Stent Symmetry Index = (maximum stent diameter - minimum stent diameter) / maximum stent diameter</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122347\">122347</a></td>\n        <td>Stent Expansion Index</td>\n        <td>Measurement of stent area relative to the reference lumen area. Stent Expansion Index = Minimum stent area / reference vessel lumen cross-sectional area</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122348\">122348</a></td>\n        <td>Lumen Shape Index</td>\n        <td>Measurement of vessel lumen eccentricity. Lumen Shape Index = (2p * sqrt(Vessel lumen cross-sectional area / p) / Lumen Perimeter) 2  Reference: Tobis &amp; Yock, “Intravascular Ultrasound Imaging”,  Chapter 7</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122350\">122350</a></td>\n        <td>Lumen Diameter Ratio</td>\n        <td>Lumen diameter ratio = minimum vessel lumen diameter / maximum vessel lumen diameter, measured at the same cross section in the vessel. Lumen diameters are measured through the center point of the lumen, which is defined as the center of gravity of the lumen area.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122351\">122351</a></td>\n        <td>Stent Diameter Ratio</td>\n        <td>Stent diameter ratio = Minimum stent diameter / Maximum stent diameter, measured at the same cross section in the vessel. Stent diameters are measured through the center point of the stent, which is defined as the center of gravity of the stent area.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122352\">122352</a></td>\n        <td>EEM Diameter Ratio</td>\n        <td>EEM diameter ratio = minimum EEM diameter / maximum EEM diameter. Measured at the same cross section in the vessel.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122354\">122354</a></td>\n        <td>Plaque Burden</td>\n        <td>Fractional area within the External Elastic Membrane (EEM) occupied by atheroma. Plaque Burden  = (EEM area - vessel lumen cross-sectional area) / EEM area</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122355\">122355</a></td>\n        <td>Arc of Calcium</td>\n        <td>Angular measurement of a Calcium deposit with the apex located at the center of the lumen, which is defined as the center of gravity of the lumen area.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122356\">122356</a></td>\n        <td>Soft plaque</td>\n        <td>Plaque characterized by low density or echogenicity.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122357\">122357</a></td>\n        <td>In-Stent Neointima</td>\n        <td>Abnormal thickening of the intima within the stented segment.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122360\">122360</a></td>\n        <td>True Lumen</td>\n        <td>Lumen surrounded by all three layers of the vessel-intima, media, and adventitia.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122361\">122361</a></td>\n        <td>False Lumen</td>\n        <td>A channel, usually parallel to the true lumen, which does not communicate with the true lumen over a portion of its length.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122363\">122363</a></td>\n        <td>Plaque Rupture</td>\n        <td>Plaque ulceration with a tear detected in a fibrous cap.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122364\">122364</a></td>\n        <td>Stent Gap</td>\n        <td>Length of gap between two consecutive stents.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122367\">122367</a></td>\n        <td>T-1 Worst</td>\n        <td>Worst stenosis - the stenosis with the smallest lumen size within a vessel segment.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122368\">122368</a></td>\n        <td>T-2 Secondary</td>\n        <td>2nd most severe stenosis within a vessel segment.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122369\">122369</a></td>\n        <td>T-3 Secondary</td>\n        <td>3rd most severe stenosis within a vessel segment.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122370\">122370</a></td>\n        <td>T-4 Secondary</td>\n        <td>4th most severe stenosis within a vessel segment.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122371\">122371</a></td>\n        <td>EEM Volume</td>\n        <td>External Elastic Membrane (EEM) volume measured within a specified region. The EEM is a discrete interface at the border between the media and the Adventitia.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122372\">122372</a></td>\n        <td>Lumen Volume</td>\n        <td>Lumen volume measured within a specified region.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122374\">122374</a></td>\n        <td>In-Stent Neointimal Volume</td>\n        <td>The amount of plaque between the lumen and stent, within the stent region; In-stent restenosis.&nbsp;In-Stent Neointimal Volume  = Stent Volume - Lumen Volume</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122375\">122375</a></td>\n        <td>Native Plaque Volume</td>\n        <td>The amount of plaque between the stent and the EEM, within the stent region.&nbsp; Native Plaque Volume = EEM Volume - Stent Volume</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122376\">122376</a></td>\n        <td>Total Plaque Volume</td>\n        <td>Total amount of plaque between the EEM and the Lumen, over the entire region that is measured.&nbsp; Total Plaque Volume = EEM Volume - Lumen Volume.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122380\">122380</a></td>\n        <td>Proximal Reference</td>\n        <td>Proximal reference segment measurement site. Typically the site with the largest lumen proximal to a stenosis but within the same segment (usually within 10 mm of the stenosis with no major intervening branches).</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122381\">122381</a></td>\n        <td>Distal Reference</td>\n        <td>Distal reference segment measurement site. Typically the site with the largest lumen distal to a stenosis but within the same segment (usually within 10 mm of the stenosis with no major intervening branches).</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122382\">122382</a></td>\n        <td>Site of Lumen Minimum</td>\n        <td>Site of the smallest lumen in a vessel, e.g., due to a stenotic lesion.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122383\">122383</a></td>\n        <td>Entire Pullback</td>\n        <td>Measurement region that encompasses the entire vessel imaged in a single pullback acquisition</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122384\">122384</a></td>\n        <td>Stented Region</td>\n        <td>Measurement region occupied by the stent</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122385\">122385</a></td>\n        <td>Proximal Stent Margin</td>\n        <td>Region starting at the proximal edge of the Stent and extending several millimeters (usually 5 mm) proximal to the Stent edge.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122386\">122386</a></td>\n        <td>Distal Stent Margin</td>\n        <td>Region starting at the distal edge of the Stent and extending several millimeters (usually 5 mm) distal to the Stent edge.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122387\">122387</a></td>\n        <td>Dissection Classification</td>\n        <td>Classification of dissections in a vessel</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122388\">122388</a></td>\n        <td>Intra-stent Dissection</td>\n        <td>Separation of neointimal hyperplasia from stent struts, usually seen only after treatment of in-stent restenosis.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122389\">122389</a></td>\n        <td>Vulnerable Plaque</td>\n        <td>Plaque with a thin cap fibrous atheroma that is at increased risk of rupture and thrombosis (or re-thrombosis) and rapid stenosis progression.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122390\">122390</a></td>\n        <td>Eroded Plaque</td>\n        <td>Plaque erosions with no structural defect (beyond endothelial injury) or gap in the plaque.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122391\">122391</a></td>\n        <td>Relative Stenosis Severity</td>\n        <td>Stenosis severity classifications of multiple lesions in a vessel.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122393\">122393</a></td>\n        <td>Restenotic Lesion</td>\n        <td>A finding of a previously treated lesion in which stenosis has reoccurred.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122394\">122394</a></td>\n        <td>Fibro-Lipidic Plaque</td>\n        <td>Loosely packed bundles of collagen fibers with regions of lipid deposition present. Region is cellular and no cholesterol clefts or necrosis are present. Some macrophage infiltration. Increase in extra cellular matrix.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122395\">122395</a></td>\n        <td>Necrotic-Lipidic Plaque</td>\n        <td>Area within the plaque with very low echogenicity separated from the lumen and surrounded by more echogenic structures (fibrous cap). Highly lipidic necrotic region with remnants of foam cells and dead lymphocytes present. No collagen fibers are visible and mechanical integrity is poor.  Cholesterol clefts and micro calcifications are visible.</td>\n       </tr>\n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122398\">122398</a></td>\n        <td>Intimal Dissection</td>\n        <td>Dissection limited to the intima or atheroma, and not extending to the media.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122399\">122399</a></td>\n        <td>Medial Dissection</td>\n        <td>Dissection in the arterial Media, extending into the media.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122400\">122400</a></td>\n        <td>Simultaneously Acquired</td>\n        <td>The referenced information was acquired simultaneously with the information in the object in which the reference occurs.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122401\">122401</a></td>\n        <td>Same Anatomy</td>\n        <td>Information acquired for the same anatomic region.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a through different anatomic tissue.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122404\">122404</a></td>\n        <td>Reconstructed</td>\n        <td>Value estimated for a vessel in the absence of a stenosis</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122405\">122405</a></td>\n        <td>Algorithm Manufacturer</td>\n        <td>Manufacturer of application used</td>\n <td><a name=\"122411\">122411</a></td>\n        <td>Threshold Value</td>\n        <td>The minimum standard deviation to define the hypokinesis and hyperkinesis</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122417\">122417</a></td>\n        <td>Regional Abnormal Wall Motion</td>\n        <td>Report of differentiation of wall motion compared to normal</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122421\">122421</a></td>\n        <td>Calibration Object</td>\n        <td>Object used for Calibration</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122422\">122422</a></td>\n        <td>Calibration Method</td>\n        <td>Method used for Calibration</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122423\">122423</a></td>\n        <td>Calibration Object Size</td>\n        <td>Size of calibration object</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122428\">122428</a></td>\n        <td>Area Length Method</td>\n        <td>Method how long axis is positioned</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122429\">122429</a></td>\n        <td>Volume Method</td>\n        <td>Model for cardiac chamber volume calculation</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122430\">122430</a></td>\n        <td>Reference Method</td>\n        <td>Method to define original diameter of the artery</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122431\">122431</a></td>\n        <td>Regression Slope ED</td>\n        <td>Relation between calculated End Diastolic volume and ventricular End Diastolic volume. The specific meaning is dependent on volume method used.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122432\">122432</a></td>\n        <td>Regression Offset ED</td>\n        <td>Correction factor for the calculated End Diastolic volume and ventricular End Diastolic volume. The specific meaning is dependent on volume method used.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122433\">122433</a></td>\n        <td>Regression Slope ES</td>\n        <td>Relation between calculated End Systolic volume and ventricular End Systolic volume. The specific meaning is dependent on volume method used.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122434\">122434</a></td>\n        <td>Regression Offset ES</td>\n        <td>Correction factor for the calculated End Systolic volume and ventricular End Systolic volume. The specific meaning is dependent on volume method used.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122435\">122435</a></td>\n        <td>Regression Volume Exponent</td>\n        <td>Exponent of volume in regression formula</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122438\">122438</a></td>\n        <td>Reference Points</td>\n        <td>Container for spatial locations or coordinates used for calculation</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122445\">122445</a></td>\n        <td>Wall Thickness</td>\n        <td>Average thickness of the chamber wall in the current view</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122446\">122446</a></td>\n        <td>Wall Volume</td>\n        <td>Volume of the chamber wall estimated from the current view</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122447\">122447</a></td>\n        <td>Wall Mass</td>\n        <td>Mass of the chamber wall (myocardium)</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122448\">122448</a></td>\n        <td>Wall Stress</td>\n        <td>Peak systolic stress of chamber wall</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122449\">122449</a></td>\n        <td>Centerline Wall Motion Analysis</td>\n        <td>Method to calculate wall motion [example: Sheehan, 1986]</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122450\">122450</a></td>\n        <td>Normalized Chord Length</td>\n        <td>The length between End Diastolic and End Systolic contour perpendicular on the centerline normalized by a method dependent ventricular perimeter length. The centerline is the line equidistant between the End Diastolic and End Systolic contour  [example: Sheehan, 1986]</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122451\">122451</a></td>\n        <td>Abnormal Region</td>\n        <td>The report of the boundaries of the abnormal (hyperkinetic, hypokinetic, a-kinetic) regions associated with the territory of the artery [example: Sheehan, 1986]</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122452\">122452</a></td>\n        <td>First Chord of Abnormal Region</td>\n        <td>The chord number specifying the begin of abnormal region [example: Sheehan, 1986]</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122453\">122453</a></td>\n        <td>Last Chord of Abnormal Region</td>\n        <td>The chord number specifying the end of abnormal region [example: Sheehan, 1986]</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122459\">122459</a></td>\n        <td>Territory Region Severity</td>\n        <td>Severity at the regional abnormality extent [example: Sheehan, 1986]</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122461\">122461</a></td>\n        <td>Opposite Region Severity</td>\n        <td>Severity at the opposite regional abnormality extent [example: Sheehan, 1986]</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122464\">122464</a></td>\n        <td>LAD Region in RAO Projection</td>\n        <td>Based on a total number of chords of 100 and RAO project the range of chords belonging to this circumferential extent lies between 5 – 85. [Sheehan, 1986]</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122465\">122465</a></td>\n        <td>RCA Region in ROA Projection</td>\n        <td>Based on a total number of chords of 100 and RAO project the range of chords belonging to this circumferential extent lies between 25 – 85. [Sheehan, 1986]</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122466\">122466</a></td>\n        <td>Single LAD Region in RAO Projection</td>\n        <td>Based on a total number of chords of 100 and RAO projection the range of chords belonging to this regional extent lies between 10 – 66 (hypokinetic) and 67 – 80 (hyperkinetic). [Sheehan, 1986]</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122467\">122467</a></td>\n        <td>Single RCA Region in RAO Projection</td>\n        <td>Based on a total number of chords of 100 and RAO projection the range of chords belonging to this regional extent lies between 51 – 80 (hypokinetic) and 10 – 50 (hyperkinetic). [Sheehan, 1986]</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122468\">122468</a></td>\n        <td>Multiple LAD Region in RAO Projection</td>\n        <td>Based on a total number of chords of 100 and RAO projection the range of chords belonging to this regional extent lies between 10 – 58 (hypokinetic) and 59 –80 (hyperkinetic). [Sheehan, 1986]</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122469\">122469</a></td>\n        <td>Multiple RCA Region in RAO Projection</td>\n        <td>Based on a total number of chords of 100 and RAO projection the range of chords belonging to this regional extent lies between 59 – 80 (hypokinetic) and 10 – 58 (hyperkinetic). [Sheehan, 1986]</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"122470\">122470</a></td>\n        <td>LAD Region in LAO Projection</td>\n        <td>Based on a total number of chords of 100 and LAO projection the range of chords belonging to this regional extent lies between 50 –100 (hypokinetic) and 20 – 49 (hyperkinetic). Acquisition protocols may be specific to a manufacturer’s product.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125204\">125204</a></td>\n        <td>Area-length biplane</td>\n        <td>Method for calculating left ventricular volume from two orthogonal views containing the true long axis (usually the apical 4 and 2 chamber views). Volume = [p L1/6]*[(4A1)¸(pL1)]*[(4A2)¸(p L2)]</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125205\">125205</a></td>\n        <td>Area-Length Single Plane</td>\n        <td>Method for calculating left ventricular volume from a view containing the true long axis (usually the apical 4-chamber view). Volume = [8(A)2]¸[3pL]</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125206\">125206</a></td>\n        <td>Cube</td>\n        <td>Method (formula) for calculating left ventricle volumes and function derivatives (EF, SV, SI, etc.) that estimates the volume as the cube of diameter.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125207\">125207</a></td>\n        <td>Method of Disks, Biplane</td>\n        <td>Method of calculating volume based on the summation of disk volumes. The disk axis is parallel to the left ventricular long axis and using a disk diameter averaged from the two chamber and four chamber views.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125208\">125208</a></td>\n        <td>Method of Disks, Single Plane</td>\n        <td>Method of calculating volume based on the summation of disk volumes. The disk axis is parallel to the left ventricular long axis with disk diameter taken from the four-chamber view.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125209\">125209</a></td>\n        <td>Teichholz</td>\n        <td>Method (formula) for calculating left ventricle volumes and function derivatives (EF, SV, SI, etc.) Volume = [7.0/(2.4+D)]*D3</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125210\">125210</a></td>\n        <td>Area by Pressure Half-Time</td>\n        <td>Mitral valve area (cm2) by Pressure Half-time = 220 (cm2.ms) / PHT (ms)</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125211\">125211</a></td>\n        <td>Biplane Ellipse</td>\n        <td>Area = P/4 X d1 X d2 d1 = anterior/posterior axis d2 = medial/lateral axis Hagen-Ansert, Sandra L., Textbook of Diagnostic Ultrasound, ed. 3, The C.V.Mosby Co., 1989, p. 73.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125212\">125212</a></td>\n        <td>Continuity Equation</td>\n        <td>For conduits in series (“in continuity”), volume flow is equal: A1*V1 = A2*V2. where V is the velocity</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125213\">125213</a></td>\n        <td>Continuity Equation by Mean Velocity</td>\n        <td>For conduits in series (“in continuity”), volume flow is equal: A1*V1 = A2*V2. where V is the mean velocity</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125214\">125214</a></td>\n        <td>Continuity Equation by Peak Velocity</td>\n        <td>For conduits in series (“in continuity”), volume flow is equal: A1*V1 = A2*V2. where V is the peak velocity</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125215\">125215</a></td>\n        <td>Continuity Equation by Velocity Time Integral</td>\n        <td>For conduits in series (“in continuity”), volume flow is equal: A1*V1 = A2*V2. where V is the velocity time integral</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125216\">125216</a></td>\n        <td>Proximal Isovelocity Surface Area</td>\n        <td>Utilizes aliasing velocity (by color Doppler) of flow into an orifice (often regurgitant or stenotic) to measure instantaneous flow rate, orifice area, and flow volume. The instantaneous flow rate = (2 π r2 vav ) * (α / π) where vav  is the constant velocity known as aliasing velocity at radius r, vp is the peak velocity at the orifice, and α is the angle in radians of the constant velocity surface. Estimated Orifice area = Flow rate / vp, where vp is the peak velocity at the orifice and the flow rate is the PISA peak flow rate. The volume flow is then the product of the orifice area and Velocity Time Integral</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125217\">125217</a></td>\n        <td>Full Bernoulli</td>\n        <td>ΔP = 4*(V12 – V22)</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125218\">125218</a></td>\n        <td>Simplified Bernoulli</td>\n        <td>ΔP = 4*V2</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125219\">125219</a></td>\n        <td>Doppler Volume Flow</td>\n        <td>Volume flow = Conduit CSA * ( Velocity Time Integral )</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125220\">125220</a></td>\n        <td>Planimetry</td>\n        <td>Direct measurement of an area by tracing an irregular perimeter</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125221\">125221</a></td>\n        <td>Left Ventricle Mass by M-mode</td>\n        <td>Mass = 1.04 * [(ST+LVID+PWT)3-LVID3] * 0.8+ 0.6. Mass unit is grams and length in cm.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125222\">125222</a></td>\n        <td>Left Ventricle Mass by Truncated Ellipse</td>\n        <td>Mass =  1.05 P ( (b + t)2 X (2/3 (a + t) + d – d3/3(a + t)2 ) – b2 (2/3a + d – d3/3a2) ) a = Semi-major axis from widest minor axis radius to apex. b = Short axis radius calculated from short axis cavity area t = Myocardial thickness calculated from short axis epicardial and cavity areas d = Truncated semi-major axis from widest short axis diameter to plane of mitral annulus. Mass unit is grams and length in cm. Schiller NB et al: Recommendations for quantification of the left ventricle by two-dimensional echocardiography, American Society of Echocardiography 2:364, 1989.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125223\">125223</a></td>\n        <td>4 Point Segment Finding Scale</td>\n        <td>A four point, echocardiographic numeric scoring scheme of myocardium segments based on evaluation of wall motion and ventricle morphology. name=\"125270\">125270</a></td>\n        <td>Left Ventricle Mass by Area Length</td>\n        <td>method to measure the mass of the Left Ventricle via the ASE area-length method at end diastole. LV Mass = 1.05*(5/6*(A1*(L+t) ) - 5/6*(A2*L) ) A1 = Left Ventricle epicardial SAX area at the level of of the papillary muscle tips at end diastole. A2 = Left Ventricle endocardial SAX area cavity area at the level of the papillary muscle tips at end diastole. L = Left Ventricle apical view long axis length at end diastole. t = Myocardial thickness can be computed as :  t = sqrt( A1/3.14) – sqrt ( A2/3.14) Reference: 1) Schiller, N.B., et al. “Recommendations for Quantification of the LV by Two-dimensional Echocardiography.&quot; J Am Soc Echo, Vol. 2, No. 5: 358-367, Sep-Oct 1989. 2) Reichek, N., et al. &quot;Anatomic Validation of Left Ventricular Mass Estimates from Clinical Two-dimensional Echocardiography: Initial Results.&quot; Circulation, Vol. 67, No. 2: 348-52, February 1983.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125271\">125271</a></td>\n        <td>Left Ventricle Mass by M-mode – adjusted by Height</td>\n        <td>Equation = Left Ventricle Mass by M-mode (in gram) / ( Height (in meter) )^2.7 Reference: Giovanni De Simone, et al. “Effect of Growth on Variability of Left Ventricular Mass: Assessment of Allometric Signals in Adults and Children and Their Capacity to Predict Cardiovascular Risk”. New York, New York and Cincinnati, Ohio.</td>\n      </tr>  \n      <tr>\n        <td><a name=\"125272\">125272</a></td>\n        <td>Left Ventricle Mass by Truncated Ellipse – adjusted by Height</td>\n        <td>Equation = Left Ventricle Mass by Truncated Ellipse / Height^2.7 Reference: Giovanni De Simone, et al. “Effect of Growth on Variability of Left Ventricular Mass: Assessment of Allometric Signals in Adults and Children and Their Capacity to Predict Cardiovascular Risk”.
